      "text": "Docker itself does not have an official, built-in TUI (Terminal User Interface). It relies primarily on its CLI (Command Line Interface) and the GUI provided by **Docker Desktop**.\n\nHowever, there is a very vibrant ecosystem of third-party TUIs.\n\n### 1. Does Docker have a TUI?\n**No, not officially.**\nIf you want a TUI experience today, most users use **`lazydocker`**. It is the most popular, free, open-source tool that wraps the Docker CLI in a navigational terminal interface.\n*   **Other options:** `dry`, `ctop` (for metrics), and `docui`.\n\n### 2. Would making a TUI break the agreement?\n**No, it would not break the agreement, provided you follow specific rules.**\nCreating a tool that interacts with the Docker Engine API or CLI is allowed and encouraged. The Docker Engine is open-source (Apache 2.0 license). However, you must be careful about **Trademarks** and **Docker Desktop** specifics.\n\nHere are the legal/agreement boundaries to watch out for:\n\n*   **The Trademark Rule (Most Important):**\n    You cannot name your tool \"Docker TUI\" or \"Docker Manager\" in a way that implies it is an official Docker product.\n    *   **Bad Name:** `DockerTUI` (Implies official status).\n    *   **Good Name:** `LazyDocker` or `ContainerTUI for Docker` (Clear it is a third-party tool).\n    *   *Docker\u0027s guidelines specifically state you should not use \"Docker\" as the first word in your project name.*\n\n*   **The Docker Desktop EULA:**\n    If your TUI relies on **Docker Desktop** (the app that runs on Mac/Windows) to run the engine, users of your tool still need to comply with the Docker Desktop license (which is paid for large companies).\n    *   Your tool itself is fine, but you cannot create a tool specifically designed to *bypass* Docker Desktop\u0027s licensing checks or replicate its proprietary paid features (like specific security scanning extensions) using reverse-engineered private APIs.\n    *   If your TUI just talks to the standard open-source Docker Engine API (which is what `lazydocker` does), you are completely safe.\n\n**Summary:** You are free to build a TUI. Just don\u0027t name it \"Docker [Something]\" and ensure you are interacting with the public Docker Engine API.",

      "text": "Yes, you can absolutely create a tool with a commercial license that requires payment for companies of a certain size (like 5+ employees).\n\nMany popular Docker-related tools use this exact business model. For example, **Portainer** is free for small setups but requires a paid license for larger business environments.\n\nHere is how to do it legally without breaking any agreements with Docker:\n\n### 1. Your code, your license\nBecause you are writing the TUI from scratch, you own the **intellectual property (IP)** of that specific code. \n*   **The Engine is Free:** The Docker Engine is licensed under **Apache 2.0**, which explicitly allows people to build commercial software on top of it.\n*   **API Usage is Permitted:** Using the Docker REST API or SDK to talk to the engine does not \"infect\" your tool with an open-source license. You are free to make your tool proprietary (closed source) or use a \"Business Source License\" (BSL) where it’s free for individuals but paid for companies.\n\n### 2. Trademark Compliance (The \"Golden Rule\")\nThe only real way you could \"break the agreement\" is by misusing the **Docker Trademark**. You cannot make it look like Docker Inc. made the tool or that it is an \"official\" part of Docker.\n*   **Prohibited Names:** *Docker TUI, Docker Pro Terminal, Official Docker Manager.*\n*   **Allowed Names:** *WhaleWatcher, ContainerDeck (compatible with Docker), MyTUI for Docker.*\n*   **The Rule of Thumb:** Do not use the word \"Docker\" as the first word of your product name.\n\n### 3. The Docker Desktop \"Gotcha\"\nYour tool is a separate entity, but your customers might be running it on top of **Docker Desktop**. \n*   **Independent Licensing:** If a company uses your TUI to manage their containers, they need to pay **you** for your TUI license AND they might still need to pay **Docker Inc.** for a Docker Desktop license (if they have \u003e250 employees).\n*   **Transparency:** It is helpful to state in your terms that your license only covers your TUI and does not include the underlying Docker Engine or Desktop software.\n\n### 4. Suggested License Types for your \"5+ Man\" Goal\nIf you want to enforce a \"pay if you\u0027re a company\" rule, consider these licensing models:\n*   **BSL (Business Source License):** Used by companies like MariaDB and Sentry. It allows the code to be public, but restricts commercial use until a certain date or under certain company-size conditions.\n*   **Dual Licensing:** The tool is open-source (GPL) for individuals/open-source projects, but companies must buy a \"Commercial License\" to use it in a closed/business environment.\n*   **Proprietary / SaaS:** You simply don\u0027t release the source code and sell it as a compiled binary with a seat-based license.\n\n**Summary:** You are completely safe to build and sell this tool. Just give it a unique name and clearly define that your license is for the *interface* you built, not the underlying Docker technology.",

      "text": "Portainer’s strategy is a textbook example of the **\"Open Core\"** business model. They didn\u0027t just build a tool; they built an ecosystem that funnels users from \"free\" to \"enterprise.\"\n\nIf you want to build a TUI and license it similarly, here is exactly how Portainer does it:\n\n### 1. The \"Open Core\" Product Split\nPortainer maintains two separate versions of the same product:\n*   **Community Edition (CE):** This is 100% open-source and free. It has all the basic features anyone needs to manage Docker. This is their **marketing engine**—it gets people hooked on the interface.\n*   **Business Edition (BE):** This is closed-source (proprietary). It includes \"Enterprise features\" that small hobbyists don\u0027t care about but big companies *require* for compliance.\n\n### 2. Feature Gating (The \"Paywall\")\nThey don\u0027t just charge for the same tool; they lock specific \"corporate\" features behind the paid license. To copy this, you would keep your TUI\u0027s basic container management free, but charge for:\n*   **RBAC (Role-Based Access Control):** Limiting which employees can click \"Delete.\"\n*   **Audit Logs:** Keeping a record of who did what (essential for security audits).\n*   **External Auth:** Integrating with Okta, Active Directory, or OAuth.\n*   **Support:** A \"guaranteed response time\" if the tool breaks.\n\n### 3. The \"3-Node\" Hook (Commercial On-Ramp)\nPortainer recently changed their strategy to be very aggressive with businesses. They offer a **\"3 Nodes Free\"** program for their **Business Edition**.\n*   **The Logic:** They let a company use the *premium* version for free on a tiny scale (3 servers). \n*   **The Trap:** Once that company grows to 4+ servers, they are already integrated into the Business Edition workflow. It is much easier for them to pay for a license than to downgrade back to the Community Edition.\n\n### 4. Legal Segmentation (The \"5-Man\" Rule)\nWhile Portainer mostly counts \"Nodes\" (servers), they also use **intent-based licensing**. Their \"Home \u0026 Student\" license specifically states:\n*   *“Restricted to Non-Commercial use. If you are a business, you cannot purchase this and keys will be revoked.”*\n*   **How you can do this:** You can use a license like the **Business Source License (BSL)**. It allows you to say: *\"This tool is free for individuals and companies with fewer than 5 employees. If you are larger, you must purchase a commercial license.\"*\n\n### 5. Independent Branding\nPortainer is very careful to stay legally safe with Docker.\n*   **The Name:** They are \"Portainer,\" not \"DockerGUI.\"\n*   **The Relationship:** They define themselves as a \"Management Platform\" that *supports* Docker, Kubernetes, and Podman. This prevents Docker Inc. from ever claiming Portainer is \"infringing\" or trying to steal their brand.\n\n### How you can apply this to your TUI:\n1.  **Name it uniquely:** Call it something like *TermiWhale* or *KnotTUI*.\n2.  **Use a dual-license:**\n    *   **GPL/MIT** for the \"Community\" version (limited features).\n    *   **Commercial EULA** for the \"Pro\" version (RBAC, Multi-user support).\n3.  **The \"5-Man\" Trigger:** In your EULA (End User License Agreement), state that use by any legal entity with \u003e5 employees requires a \"Pro\" subscription.\n4.  **Enforcement:** You can use a simple API check in the TUI that requires a license key for \"Pro\" features, or simply rely on the \"honor system\" for companies (most legitimate 5+ man companies will pay to avoid legal risk).\n\n**Summary:** Portainer wins by being the \"friendly face\" of Docker that eventually becomes a \"security gatekeeper\" for corporations. You can do the same with a TUI by focusing on **multi-user/security features** as your paid tier.",

The \"Permissive\" Stack\nBoth `clap` and `ratatui` use the **MIT/Apache 2.0** dual license.\n*   **What this means for you:** You can use them to build closed-source, proprietary, or commercially licensed software. You are not forced to share your source code (unlike the GPL license).\n*   **The Missing Piece:** To talk to Docker, you should use the **`bollard`** crate. It is the most modern, async-friendly Docker API client for Rust and is also licensed under Apache 2.0.\n\n### 2. How to implement the \"5+ person company\" rule\nSince your code is your own property, you can license it however you want. To achieve the \"Pay if you\u0027re a big company\" goal, you have two main options:\n\n#### Option A: The \"Business Source License\" (BSL)\nThis is what companies like Sentry and MariaDB use. \n*   **The Rule:** The code is public, and anyone can use it for free (individuals, small teams).\n*   **The Trigger:** Use by a company with more than X employees requires a commercial subscription. \n*   **The Conversion:** After a set time (e.g., 3 years), that specific version of the code automatically becomes open-source (GPL or MIT). This builds trust with users.\n\n#### Option B: Dual Licensing (The Portainer Model)\n*   **Version 1 (Community):** Free, open-source, limited features (no \"pro\" features like team-based logs or advanced networking).\n*   **Version 2 (Pro):** A compiled binary that requires a license key. You include a clause in your EULA stating: *\"Commercial entities with 5 or more employees must use the Pro version.\"*\n\n### 3. Technical Implementation in Rust\nIf you want to actually \"enforce\" the license rather than just relying on the honor system, here is how you do it in a TUI:\n\n*   **License Management:** Look at the **`keygen-rs`** crate. It’s an unofficial SDK for *Keygen.sh*, a service that handles license key validation, machine activation, and \"seats\" for you.\n*   **Offline Check:** You can bake a public key into your Rust binary to verify digitally signed license files, so your TUI doesn\u0027t need to \"call home\" to the internet every single time it starts.\n*   **Obfuscation:** Because Rust compiles to a native binary, it is much harder to \"crack\" than a Python or Node.js tool, which makes your commercial license easier to protect.\n\n### 4. Summary Checklist for Success\n1.  **Name:** Give it a cool, unique name (e.g., `Dockey`, `WhaleTerm`, `Hull`). Do **not** name it \"Docker TUI.\"\n2.  **SDK:** Use `clap` (args), `ratatui` (UI), and `bollard` (Docker connection).\n3.  **License File:** Create a `LICENSE` file in your repo that clearly defines the \"5-person\" restriction. \n4.  **The Docker Agreement:** As long as you don\u0027t pretend to be Docker Inc. and don\u0027t use their official logos in your marketing as if you\u0027re \"authorized\" by them, you are 100% in the clear.\n\n**Verdict:** Go for it.       "text": "This strategy is called **\"Source Available\"** (as opposed to \"Open Source\"). It is a very effective way for a solo developer to keep the community happy while making sure that profitable companies pay their fair share.\n\nSince you want the tool to be **fully featured for everyone** but legally require a license for companies of a certain size, here is the exact legal and technical blueprint for doing that.\n\n### 1. The Best License for You: BSL 1.1\nThe **Business Source License (BSL) 1.1** (used by MariaDB, Sentry, and HashiCorp) is perfect for your goal. It is not technically \"Open Source\" by the OSI definition, but it is \"Source Available.\"\n\n*   **How it works:** You provide the source code for everyone to see and modify. However, you add an **\"Additional Use Grant\"** that defines who gets it for free.\n*   **Your 5-Man Clause:** You would write your license like this:\n    \u003e *\"Use of the software is free for individuals and for entities with fewer than 5 employees. Use of the software by any entity with 5 or more employees requires a commercial license.\"*\n*   **The \"Conversion\" Clause:** To keep the community\u0027s trust, the BSL requires you to pick a date (e.g., 3 years from now) when that specific version of the code automatically converts to a fully Open Source license (like Apache 2.0).\n\n### 2. Alternative: The PolyForm Small Business License\nIf you don\u0027t want the complexity of the BSL, look at the **PolyForm Project**. They have a \"Small Business\" license specifically designed for this:\n*   **The Logic:** It allows free use for \"Small Businesses\" (defined by you, e.g., \u003c 5 people or \u003c $1M revenue) but requires a paid agreement for everyone else.\n\n### 3. Will this break the \"Docker Agreement\"?\n**No, as long as you respect the Trademark.**\nDocker Inc. does not care how you license your tool. They only care about their brand.\n*   **The Name Test:** You cannot name it `DockerTUI`. You should name it something like `WhaleGate` or `Ratadock` and state in the description: *\"A TUI for managing Docker containers.\"*\n*   **Compatibility:** Your tool is a \"client\" of their engine. Just like a Twitter client isn\u0027t owned by Twitter, a Docker TUI isn\u0027t owned by Docker.\n\n### 4. How to \"Enforce\" it as a Solo Dev\nSince you aren\u0027t a big company with a sales team, you have two options for enforcement:\n\n#### Option A: The \"Honor System\" (EULA Only)\nYou simply state the rules in your `LICENSE` and `README`.\n*   **Why it works:** Most 5+ person companies have legal departments. They do not want to risk a lawsuit or a \"license audit\" for a $50/year tool. They will buy the license just to be \"compliant.\"\n*   **Pros:** Zero coding required.\n*   **Cons:** Some people will ignore it.\n\n#### Option B: The \"Soft Lock\" (License Key)\nWhen the TUI starts, it checks for a `.license` file in the user\u0027s home directory.\n*   **Implementation:** \n    1.  If no key is found, show a small message at the bottom: *\"Free for individuals/small teams. Support development: [link]\"*\n    2.  If the user wants to \"Register\" as a company, they enter a key that removes the message.\n*   **Pros:** Reminds users that they should pay if they are a company.\n*   **Cons:** You have to build a small payment/key generation site (using something like Stripe or LemonSqueezy).\n\n### 5. Technical Stack Advice (Rust)\nSince you are using `clap` and `ratatui`, your binary will be a single file. This is a **huge selling point** for companies.\n*   **Distribution:** Use `cargo-dist` to generate binaries for Mac, Windows, and Linux.\n*   **Security:** Because you are compiled to machine code, your \"license check\" logic is much harder to bypass than if you were using Python or Node.js.\n\n### Summary Checklist\n1.  **Select a License:** BSL 1.1 with a \"5-employee\" additional grant.\n2.  **Pick a Unique Name:** Avoid starting with \"Docker.\"\n3.  **Create a \"Buy a License\" Page:** Use a simple service like **LemonSqueezy**—they handle the \"Tax/VAT\" for you, which is the biggest headache of selling to international companies.\n4.  **Put it on GitHub:** Keep the code public. It builds trust and acts as your best marketing tool.",

      "text": "Your **Dracon License v1.0** is perfectly fine for this project and **does not break any agreement with Docker.** \n\nSince you have already decided against the BSL (because you don\u0027t want the \"eventually open source\" clause), this proprietary \"Source Available\" model is the correct path for your goals.\n\nHere is the breakdown of why this works with Docker and what you need to be careful about:\n\n### 1. Docker Compatibility\nDocker (the company) does not restrict what license you use for tools that interact with their engine. \n*   **The Engine is a \"Dependency\":** Just because your TUI talks to the Docker API doesn\u0027t mean your TUI has to follow Docker\u0027s open-source license.\n*   **Commercial Freedom:** You are legally allowed to sell a proprietary \"lens\" (the TUI) that looks at an open-source \"engine\" (Docker).\n\n### 2. The \"Trademark\" Red Line\nThe only way your license or product would \"break the agreement\" with Docker is if your branding is confusing.\n*   **The Conflict:** If you name your tool **\"Docker Pro TUI\"** and use the **Dracon License** (which requires payment), Docker Inc. could argue that you are selling \"Docker\" software under your own name.\n*   **The Solution:** Use your brand name first. **\"Azumi: A Terminal Manager for Docker\"** is 100% safe. **\"Docker Manager by Azumi\"** is risky.\n\n### 3. Upstream License Compliance (`ratatui`, `clap`, `bollard`)\nBecause you are using Rust crates that are MIT/Apache 2.0, you are allowed to put them inside a proprietary product (Dracon License). However, those licenses require you to **keep the original copyright notices.**\n*   **Action:** In your TUI\u0027s \"About\" or \"Legal\" screen, you must include a list of the libraries you used and their licenses. This is standard for all commercial software.\n\n### 4. Refining your License for a TUI\nYour current license wording is strong, but for a **TUI tool**, section 1.2 (\"Production Use\") can be a bit blurry. \n\nIn the software world:\n*   **Production Use** usually means \"running on a server to serve customers.\" \n*   **TUIs** are usually \"Utility Tools\" (like an IDE or a Terminal). \n\n**Recommendation:** You might want to clarify Section 1.2 to include **\"Commercial/Professional Use.\"**\n*   *Current:* \"A Commercial License is required... for Production Use.\"\n*   *Suggested Addition:* \"...or for use in a professional capacity by an employee of a covered organization.\"\n*   **Why?** A developer at a big company might argue, *\"I\u0027m only using this TUI to look at my local dev containers, not \u0027Production,\u0027 so I don\u0027t have to pay.\"* If you want them to pay, make sure the license covers \"use within a company with 5+ employees\" regardless of whether they are touching a production server.\n\n### 5. Why your \"Anti-Competition\" Clause (Section 2.1) is smart\nSince your code is \"Source Available\" (people can see the Rust code on GitHub), your **Section 2.1 (Competitive Use)** is vital. \n*   It prevents a larger company from forking your `ratatui` code, stripping out your \"Dracon\" branding, and releasing their own \"WhaleUI\" using your hard work. \n\n### Final Verdict:\nYou are in the clear. Your stack (`clap` + `ratatui` + `bollard`) is technically excellent for this, and your **Dracon License v1.0** provides the legal protection you want to ensure that if a company is getting value out of your tool, they are paying for it.\n\n**Next Step Recommendation:** \nWhen you build the TUI, include a `LICENSE` command (e.g., `azumi --license`) that prints your Dracon License text. This makes it impossible for a company to claim they \"didn\u0027t see\" the terms.",

      "text": "The transition from a specialized Docker tool to an \"ultimate\" command center named **Tiles** is a brilliant strategic move. It moves your product from being a \"competitor to a free tool\" (Lazydocker) to being a \"unique workspace\" that doesn\u0027t exist yet in the terminal.\n\nHere is why this works and how it stays within the legal/agreement boundaries:\n\n### 1. The Name: \"Tiles\" is Perfect\nFrom a trademark perspective, **Tiles** is a safe and strong name.\n*   **No Trademark Risk:** It contains no reference to Docker, so you are 100% safe from Docker Inc.’s legal team.\n*   **Branding:** The name \"Tiles\" perfectly describes a TUI layout where the screen is split into different panes (files, containers, CPU). It suggests organization and a \"tiling window manager\" experience inside the terminal.\n*   **Uniqueness:** While there are many \"tile\" crates for game dev, there is no major \"Tiles\" system manager. You can own this brand.\n\n### 2. The \"Command Center\" Strategy\nBy combining **Files + Docker + System Resources**, you are building a \"Terminal Dashboard.\" This is a massive value proposition for developers who usually have to keep 3 tabs open:\n*   **Tab 1:** `yazi` or `ranger` (File Manager)\n*   **Tab 2:** `lazydocker` (Containers)\n*   **Tab 3:** `btop` or `htop` (System Monitor)\n\nIf **Tiles** puts all of these in one view (or easily switchable \"tiles\"), it becomes an essential productivity tool.\n\n### 3. Does this break the Docker Agreement?\n**Absolutely not.** \nYour tool is now even *further* away from being a \"Docker clone.\" It is a general-purpose system utility that *happens* to have a Docker module.\n*   **The \"Module\" Approach:** You can treat Docker as an optional \"plugin\" or \"pane\" within Tiles. This makes it clear to users (and to Docker Inc.) that you are a separate platform providing an integration, not a copycat product.\n*   **Commercial License (Dracon v1.0):** Your license fits this perfectly. A company with 5+ employees using a \"System Dashboard\" to manage their servers and local files is exactly the kind of professional user who expects to pay for high-quality software.\n\n### 4. Technical Blueprint for \"Tiles\" (Rust Stack)\nSince you are using `ratatui`, you can leverage its layout system to create the \"tiles.\" Here is the library stack you’ll want:\n\n*   **File Manager Pane:** Use `walkdir` or `jwalk` for fast directory traversal and `std::fs` for file operations.\n*   **Docker Pane:** Continue using `bollard`. It is the most robust way to get container data asynchronously.\n*   **System Resources Pane:** Use the **`sysinfo`** crate. It’s the gold standard in Rust for getting CPU, RAM, and Disk usage across Linux, Mac, and Windows.\n*   **Layout:** Ratatui’s `Layout` and `Constraint` modules are designed exactly for this \"tiling\" look.\n\n### 5. Why the \"Ultimate\" approach is better for your business\n*   **Higher Stickiness:** If a developer starts their day by opening `tiles`, and they use it to navigate files *and* check their containers, they will never close it. It becomes their \"Home\" in the terminal.\n*   **Justifiable Pricing:** It is much easier to ask a 5-man company for money for a \"complete terminal workspace\" than for just a Docker TUI. You are selling a tool that replaces three other tools.\n\n### Summary\n**Tiles** is a \"Terminal File \u0026 System Command Center.\" \n*   **Agreement Status:** 100% Compliant. \n*   **Market Position:** Higher value than a simple TUI. \n*   **Action:** Proceed with **Tiles** under your **Dracon License**. \n\nThis shifts your product from a \"helper utility\" to \"critical infrastructure\" for developers. That is where the money is.",

Legal Verification: \"Commercializing Open Source\"\nSince you are using `clap`, `ratatui`, `bollard`, and `sysinfo`, you are building on **MIT** and **Apache 2.0** foundations. \n*   **The Law:** These licenses specifically allow \"Commercial Use.\" You can take these libraries, build a proprietary product (Tiles), and sell it without sharing your own source code.\n*   **The Requirement (Attribution):** The only thing you *must* do is include the original copyright notice of those crates. \n    *   **Pro Tip:** In your TUI, add a \"Credits\" or \"Legal\" section (e.g., `tiles --version` or a `?` help menu) that lists: *\"This software uses Ratatui (MIT), Clap (Apache 2.0)...\"* This satisfies 100% of your legal obligations to the open-source community.\n\n### 2. Why \"Tiles\" is the \"Ultimate\" Commercial Play\nMost TUI tools are **utilities** (you open them, do one thing, and close them). **Tiles** is an **environment** (you open it and leave it open all day).\n\nThis distinction is huge for your **Dracon License**:\n*   **High Value for Companies:** Companies pay for \"Workspaces\" (like Slack, VS Code, or JetBrains). By combining Files + Docker + System, you aren\u0027t just a tool; you are the **operating system of the terminal.**\n*   **The License Trigger:** When a manager sees a developer using **Tiles** all day every day, they see it as a \"Professional Tool.\" They are much more likely to approve a commercial license for a 5+ person team because it’s clearly \"essential infrastructure.\"\n\n### 3. Finally, I\u0027ve landed on a commercial licensing model with a \"Dracon License v1.0\" - free for individuals and small teams, paid for larger entities.\n\n\n**Refining Strategy \u0026 Features**\n\nI\u0027m now zeroing in on Tiles\u0027 strategic position. My main competition consists of Yazi/Ranger for files, Lazydocker for Docker, and Btop/Htop for the system. I see Tiles as the \"Context Switcher Killer,\" a tool that does all of these things. Core pillars remain file management, container orchestration, and system monitoring. I\u0027m focusing on \"The Unified Pane,\" interconnectedness, and the command palette for phase 1.\n\n\n**Defining Next Phases \u0026 Sales**\n\nI\u0027ve fleshed out Phase 2 as a built-in terminal, avoiding context switching. Phase 3 targets remote management, particularly for Docker and Kubernetes, ideal for larger teams and the paid tier. My sales pitch will emphasize productivity (\"stop alt-tabbing\") and simplicity (\"one binary, zero dependencies\"). I\u0027m also considering log aggregation, port management, and a Git status indicator for file tiles. The Command Palette will be essential.\n\n\n**Optimizing Performance \u0026 UX**\n\nI\u0027m now prioritizing performance and user experience. Speed is paramount; Rust must feel instantaneous. To enhance usability, I plan to allow extensive customization of tile configurations through YAML or TOML. Finally, I\u0027m envisioning a \"Zen\" mode that streamlines the interface, revealing only the essential elements for distraction-free work.\n\n\n",

      "text": "To make **Tiles** a successful commercial product, you need to move beyond just \"showing\" data. The strategy should be to make it the **\"Glue\"** for a developer’s workflow. \n\nCurrently, developers \"Alt-Tab\" between a file manager, a terminal, and a browser. **Tiles** wins if it eliminates that friction.\n\nHere is the best strategy and a list of high-value features to add:\n\n---\n\n### 1. The Strategy: \"The Context-Aware Workspace\"\nDon\u0027t just show Files, Docker, and System as separate boxes. Make them **talk to each other.**\n*   **The Workflow:** If I highlight a `Dockerfile` in the **File Tile**, the **Docker Tile** should automatically highlight the corresponding image or container.\n*   **The Action:** If I see a process hogging CPU in the **System Tile**, I should be able to press a key to see which **Docker Container** it belongs to or where its binary is in the **File Tile**.\n*   **Why this works:** This \"interconnectivity\" is something `htop` or `lazydocker` can’t do because they only see their own world.\n\n---\n\n### 2. High-Value Features to Add\n\nTo justify a commercial license for a 5+ person company, you need features that scream **Professional Productivity**:\n\n#### A. The \"Log Streamer\" (Crucial)\nInstead of just seeing that a container is \"Running,\" add a Tile for **Aggregated Logs**. \n*   Allow users to \"Pin\" logs from a specific file, a specific Docker container, and a system service into one scrolling view. \n\n#### B. Network \u0026 Ports Tile\nDevelopers are constantly asking: *\"Why is this port busy?\"*\n*   Add a tile that shows **Listening Ports**.\n*   Let users \"Kill\" the process sitting on a port directly from the UI.\n*   Link it to Docker: \"Port 8080 is being held by Docker Container `web-server`.\"\n\n#### C. The \"Command Palette\" (`Ctrl+P`)\nSince the terminal can get cluttered, add a global search.\n*   Type `Ctrl+P` and search for a filename, a container name, or a process ID. \n*   This makes **Tiles** feel like VS Code but for the terminal.\n\n#### D. Git Integration (Lite)\nYou don’t need to be a full Git GUI, but the **File Tile** should show:\n*   File status (Modified/Added/Untracked) via color coding.\n*   Current branch name at the bottom of the tile.\n*   This prevents the user from having to run `git status` constantly.\n\n#### E. Remote Support (The \"Pro\" Feature)\nThis is what will get companies to pay.\n*   Allow **Tiles** to connect to a remote server via **SSH**.\n*   The user sees their local files on the left and the remote server\u0027s Docker/System status on the right.\n*   Managing remote production environments from a local TUI is a \"killer app\" feature.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Business Strategy: The \"Zero-Config\" Pitch\n\nLarge companies hate complex setup. Your strategy for **Tiles** should be **\"The Zero-Config Dashboard.\"**\n\n1.  **Single Binary:** \"Download `tiles`, chmod +x, and you have a full dev ops suite.\" No Python, no Node, no dependencies.\n2.  **Performance:** Since you are using Rust, emphasize that **Tiles** uses \u003c 20MB of RAM. Developers hate Electron apps (like Docker Desktop) because they eat 2GB of RAM. **Tiles is the \"Green\" alternative.**\n3.  **Custom Layouts (The YAML Hook):**\n    *   Allow users to save a `tiles.toml` file in a project folder.\n    *   When they run `tiles` in that folder, it opens the exact panes they need for that project (e.g., File pane on the left, Logs on the bottom, Docker on the right).\n\n---\n\n### 4. How to Handle the \"5+ Person\" License\nSince your **Dracon License** relies on the number of employees:\n\n*   **The \"Telemetry\" Choice:** You can choose to have **zero telemetry** (total privacy). This is a huge selling point for security-conscious companies. \n*   **The \"Honor System\" + Watermark:** For the free version, you could have a very small, dim text at the bottom: `Tiles Free Edition`. When they enter a commercial key, it disappears and says `Licensed to [Company Name]`.\n*   **Corporate Sales:** Create a simple \"Buy\" button on your site that generates a license key via **Stripe** or **LemonSqueezy**.\n\n### Summary of the \"Tiles\" Evolution:\n1.  **File Manager:** Navigate and edit.\n2.  **Docker Manager:** Control and monitor.\n3.  **System Manager:** CPU/RAM/Network.\n4.  **The Bridge:** Make them interactive (File -\u003e Docker -\u003e Process).\n5.  **The Workspace:** Save layouts per project.\n\n**Final Thought:** If you build this, you aren\u0027t just making a TUI; you are making a **Terminal IDE for DevOps.** That is a very high-value product that 5+ person companies will gladly pay for to save their developers\u0027 time.",

      "text": "If you make **Tiles** the \"ultimate\" terminal workspace, its worth isn\u0027t just the price tag you put on it—it is measured by the **Return on Investment (ROI)** for the companies that buy it. \n\nBased on current developer tool benchmarks and productivity data, here is an analysis of what **Tiles** could be worth and how to price it for different company sizes.\n\n### 1. The \"Productivity Math\" (The ROI)\nTo convince a company to pay, you show them how much money they are losing without your tool.\n*   **The Problem:** Research shows developers lose **5–15 hours per week** to \"unproductive work\" (context switching, gathering context, and waiting on tools). \n*   **The Cost:** At an average senior developer rate of **$83/hour**, a company loses roughly **$250 per developer, per day** to context switching.\n*   **The Tiles Value:** If **Tiles** saves a developer just **15 minutes a day** by keeping them in one unified TUI (Files + Docker + System), it saves the company **$400+ per month per developer**.\n\n### 2. Suggested Pricing Tiers (Market-Aligned)\nGiven that Tiles is \"Ultimate\" (replacing 3+ tools), you can price it at the top of the market for TUI tools.\n\n| Tier | Company Size | Recommended Price | Why this price? |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **Personal** | \u003c 5 Employees | **Free** | Per your Dracon License. Builds a massive fan base. |\n| **Professional** | 5 – 50 Employees | **$12 – $18 /user/mo** | Aligns with **GitKraken** and **Warp Build**. It\u0027s an easy \"no-brainer\" for managers. |\n| **Business** | 50 – 250 Employees | **$30 – $45 /user/mo** | Aligns with **Warp Business**. Includes SSO, Team Configs, and Priority Support. |\n| **Enterprise** | 250+ Employees | **Contact Sales** | Usually includes volume discounts, but requires custom security audits and SLAs. |\n\n### 3. What makes it \"Ultimate\" (Roadmap to 10x Value)\nTo justify the $45/month price point, you need to add \"Corporate-grade\" features that separate you from free tools like `lazydocker` or `yazi`:\n\n*   **The \"Remote\" Tile:** Let users view Docker and Files on a remote server via SSH as if it were local. This is a massive \"Pro\" feature for DevOps.\n*   **The \"Kubernetes\" Tile:** If you add K8s support (like `k9s`), you move into a much higher spending bracket. Companies pay significantly more for Kubernetes management than for Docker.\n*   **The \"Scripting\" Tile:** Allow users to pin custom shell scripts as \"Tiles.\" (e.g., a \"Deploy\" button in a tile).\n*   **Project Contexts:** Automatically switch layouts when the user `cd`s into a different project folder (detected via `.tiles.toml`).\n\n### 4. Comparison to Competitors\n*   **Sublime Text/Merge:** Charges **$99** for a personal license and roughly **$65/seat/year** for business.\n*   **Portainer:** Can cost **$995+/year** for small teams just for the Docker management part.\n*   **Warp:** A modern terminal that charges **$45/user/month** for its top business tier.\n\n### 5. Strategy: The \"Seat\" vs. \"Entity\" Trigger\nYour Dracon License uses an **Employee Count Trigger**, which is very smart.\n*   **For a 10-man team:** If they buy 10 seats at $15/mo, that\u0027s **$1,800/year** in revenue for you from just one small office.\n*   **For a 200-man team:** If they buy 200 seats at the Business tier ($35/mo), that\u0027s **$84,000/year** from a single customer.\n\n### Summary of Worth\nIf you build **Tiles** to be the \"Home\" of the terminal:\n1.  **To the Individual:** It is worth **infinite** value (free, high productivity).\n2.  **To a 10-man Startup:** It is worth **$1,500 - $2,000/year** to keep their team focused and fast.\n3.  **To you (The Creator):** With just 100 small business customers (10 devs each), you are looking at **$150,000+ ARR** (Annual Recurring Revenue).\n\n**Final Tip:** Don\u0027t underprice. If **Tiles** truly becomes the \"Ultimate\" tool, you are selling **time**. Companies have huge budgets to buy back their developers\u0027 time.",

      "text": "This is a great strategy. \"Per-seat\" pricing is often what scares companies off because it creates a constant administrative headache (they have to add/remove users every time someone joins or leaves).\n\nBy offering **Fixed Tiers based on Company Size**, you become the \"easy choice\" for a manager. They don\u0027t have to count heads; they just know \"we are a 20-person company, so we pay the $X flat fee.\"\n\nHere is a recommended pricing structure for **Tiles** that uses standard industry \"bands\" and \"click-to-buy\" price points.\n\n### 1. The \"Fixed Size\" Pricing Tiers\nThese bands are based on standard business firmographics (how governments and tax offices categorize companies).\n\n| Tier | Company Size | Yearly Flat Fee (Recommended) | Monthly Equivalent |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **Personal** | \u003c 5 Employees | **Free** | $0 |\n| **Small Team** | 5 – 20 Employees | **$290 / year** | ~$24/mo |\n| **Growth** | 21 – 100 Employees | **$950 / year** | ~$79/mo |\n| **Corporate** | 101 – 500 Employees | **$2,450 / year** | ~$204/mo |\n| **Enterprise** | 500+ Employees | **$5,000 / year** | Flat fee for the whole org |\n\n### 2. Why this works (The \"No-Brainer\" Pitch)\n*   **Zero Admin:** The manager doesn\u0027t have to manage seats. They buy one license key, and anyone in the company can use it.\n*   **Budget Predictability:** Finance departments love this. They know exactly what the cost will be for the next 12 months, regardless of how many developers they hire.\n*   **The \"Click to Buy\" Flow:** Use a service like **LemonSqueezy** or **Stripe Tax**. You just put five \"Buy Now\" buttons on your site. The user clicks, pays, and gets a license key emailed instantly.\n\n### 3. Implementing the \"Buy\" Button\nTo keep it simple:\n1.  **Checkout:** When they click \"Buy,\" they enter their company name and email.\n2.  **The Key:** You generate a cryptographically signed license file or string (e.g., `DRACON-TILES-ABC-123`).\n3.  **Activation:** In the **Tiles** TUI, they can run a command like `tiles --license [KEY]` or just drop a `license.txt` in the config folder.\n\n### 4. How the TUI \"Enforces\" This\nSince you want to be \"friendly\" and not \"scary,\" use **Soft Enforcement**:\n*   **The \"Free\" Experience:** If no license is found, the TUI works 100% perfectly. At the bottom of the screen, in a very dim color, it says: *\"Free for \u003c5 employees. Support Tiles at dracon.uk\"*\n*   **The \"Licensed\" Experience:** Once they buy the $290/year license, that text disappears. It might be replaced by a small, proud badge: `[ Licensed to Acme Corp ]`.\n*   **Psychology:** In a company of 20 people, the CTO or Lead Dev will see that \"Support Tiles\" message every day. They will feel guilty *not* paying $290 (which is less than the cost of one team lunch) to support a tool they use all day.\n\n### 5. Strategy: The \"One-Time\" vs. \"Yearly\" Choice\nFor a tool like **Tiles**, you could even offer a **Lifetime Buy** for small teams:\n*   *\"Pay $499 once, and your team of \u003c20 has it forever.\"*\n*   **Pro:** Immediate cash flow for you.\n*   **Con:** No recurring revenue. \n*   **Recommendation:** Stick to **Yearly**. It’s the standard for professional dev tools, and it ensures you have money to keep maintaining the Docker/System integrations as APIs change.\n\n### Summary\nIf you use this \"Fixed Tier\" model, you aren\u0027t a \"salesperson\"—you are providing a **subscription to productivity.**\n1.  **5-20 band:** Your \"sweet spot.\" There are millions of these companies.\n2.  **No Seat Tracking:** This is your biggest competitive advantage over tools like Docker Desktop or Slack.\n3.  **The Dracon License:** Your v1.0 license already supports this. You just need to list these prices on your website.\n\n**Ready to launch?** Just build the \"Buy\" buttons. Companies would much rather \"click and buy\" a flat fee than \"talk to sales\" for a per-seat quote.",

Executive Summary\nTiles is a high-performance, unified terminal workspace designed to be the \"Ultimate Command Center\" for developers and DevOps engineers. Instead of switching between a file manager (`yazi`), a Docker monitor (`lazydocker`), and a system monitor (`btop`), Tiles combines these into a single, context-aware, tiling interface.\n\n## 2. Core Philosophy \u0026 Strategy\n*   **The \"Glue\" Strategy:** Unlike standalone tools, Tiles is context-aware. Selecting a file in the File Tile should provide relevant context in the Docker or System tiles (e.g., highlighting the container associated with a specific project folder).\n*   **High Performance:** Built in Rust for near-zero latency and minimal RAM footprint (\u003c20MB). \n*   **Zero-Config Dashboard:** A single binary that \"just works\" but can be customized via a `tiles.toml` project file.\n*   **Commercial Intent:** Designed to be a professional-grade tool. We follow a \"Fixed Tier\" pricing model for companies to ensure predictable costs and zero administrative overhead.\n\n## 3. Key Modules (The \"Tiles\")\n*   **File Tile:** A high-speed navigator with basic CRUD operations and Git status integration.\n*   **Docker Tile:** Full lifecycle management (start/stop/logs/stats) using the `bollard` crate to interface directly with the Docker Engine API.\n*   **System Tile:** Real-time monitoring of CPU, RAM, Network, and Disk usage via the `sysinfo` crate.\n*   **Interactivity:** Tiles must support a \"Zoom\" feature (expanding one tile to full screen) and global search (Command Palette).\n\n## 4. Technical Constraints for AI\n*   **UI Framework:** Use `ratatui` with an emphasis on a responsive layout system.\n*   **Asynchronous Logic:** All data fetching (Docker/System) must be handled asynchronously (Tokio) to prevent UI freezing.\n*   **Licensing Implementation:** The code must remain \"Source Available\" but include a \"Soft Lock\" or license check for the Dracon v1.0 5-man rule.\n*   **Branding:** Always refer to the product as \"Tiles.\" Do not use \"Docker\" as the primary name to respect trademarks.\n\n## 5. Vision for Future Features\n*   SSH/Remote server monitoring (The \"Pro\" feature).\n*   Log Aggregator (Streaming logs from files and containers into one view).\n*   Kubernetes (K8s) pane for enterprise scalability.\n\n***\n\n### How to use this with an AI:\n1.  **Start a new chat.**\n2.  **Paste the text above.**\n3.  **Add your specific request at the end**, such as:\n    *   *\"Can you help me design the `App` struct that handles the state for these three tiles using Ratatui?\"*\n    *   *\"How should I structure the async loop for the Docker data using the `bollard` crate so it doesn\u0027t lag the UI?\"*\n    *   *\"Write a license check function that prints the Dracon v1.0 disclaimer when the tool starts.\"*",

      "text": "This is the **Master Architecture Document**. It is designed to be pasted into an AI (like Claude 3.5 Sonnet, GPT-4o, or Cursor) to give it a complete mental model of the entire project—from the Rust structs to the business strategy.\n\nThis is 10x more detailed than the previous summary. It includes **data structures**, **UI logic**, and **commercial implementation details**.\n\n***\n\n# 🏗️ MASTER PLAN: PROJECT TILES\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Draft)  \n**Legal:** Dracon License v1.0 (Proprietary / Source Available)  \n**Stack:** Rust, Ratatui, Tokio, Bollard, Sysinfo.\n\n## 1. 🌍 The High-Level Vision\n**Tiles** is a \"Terminal Workspace Environment.\" It is not just a monitoring tool; it is an interactive operating system for the terminal. It solves the context-switching problem by unifying **Files**, **Containers**, and **System Resources** into a single, tiling pane interface that supports cross-module context (e.g., selecting a directory filters the Docker view).\n\n**Business Goal:** To capture the 5+ employee company market with a fixed-tier license model by offering a tool that replaces `lazydocker`, `ranger`, and `btop` combined.\n\n---\n\n## 2. 🏛️ Technical Architecture (Rust)\n\n### A. The Core Event Loop (`main.rs`)\nThe application must run on a **Dual-Threaded Async Architecture**:\n1.  **Main Thread (UI):** Synchronous. Handles drawing to the terminal via `Ratatui` and capturing user keyboard input via `Crossterm`.\n2.  **Background Runtime (Tokio):** Asynchronous. Handles heavy lifting (Docker API calls, File I/O, System polling) to ensure the UI never freezes.\n3.  **Communication:** Use `tokio::sync::mpsc` channels to pass messages from Background -\u003e UI (e.g., `DockerContainerUpdated(Vec\u003cContainerSummary\u003e)`).\n\n### B. State Management (`app.rs`)\nThe Global State must be centralized. Do not scatter state across widgets.\n\n```rust\npub struct App {\n    pub running: bool,\n    pub active_tile: TileType, // Enum: Files, Docker, System, Logs\n    pub mode: AppMode,         // Enum: Normal, Input, Zoomed\n    \n    // The Data Stores\n    pub file_state: FileState,\n    pub docker_state: DockerState,\n    pub system_state: SystemState,\n    \n    // Commercial / Config\n    pub config: Config, // Loaded from tiles.toml\n    pub license: LicenseStatus, // Enum: Free, Commercial(Key)\n}\n\npub enum LicenseStatus {\n    FreeMode,           // Show \"Support Tiles\" footer\n    Commercial(String), // Hide footer, show Company Name\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. 🧩 The Modules (The \"Tiles\")\n\n### Tile 1: The File Manager (`modules/files.rs`)\n*   **Library:** `std::fs`, `walkdir`.\n*   **Visuals:** Tree view or List view.\n*   **Features:**\n    *   Vim navigation (`j`/`k`).\n    *   **Git Integration:** Show `[+]`, `[-]`, `[M]` next to files using `libgit2` or CLI parsing.\n    *   **Context Trigger:** When a user hovers a folder containing a `Dockerfile` or `docker-compose.yml`, emit a `ContextEvent::ProjectSelected(path)` signal.\n\n### Tile 2: The Docker Manager (`modules/docker.rs`)\n*   **Library:** `bollard` (Async).\n*   **Visuals:** Table view (Containers) + Sparklines (Stats).\n*   **Features:**\n    *   **Listing:** ID, Image, Status, Ports, CPU%.\n    *   **Actions:** `s` (start), `x` (stop), `r` (restart), `l` (logs), `e` (exec shell).\n    *   **Reactive Filtering:** If `ContextEvent` is received, filter the list to only show containers related to the current file path (project).\n\n### Tile 3: The System Monitor (`modules/system.rs`)\n*   **Library:** `sysinfo`.\n*   **Visuals:** Gauges (Ratatui) and Sparklines for history.\n*   **Features:**\n    *   Global CPU/RAM usage.\n    *   **Process List:** List top 10 processes.\n    *   **Port Watcher:** List active listening ports (TCP).\n\n### Tile 4: The Command Center (The \"Glue\")\n*   **Visuals:** A popup modal (like VS Code Command Palette).\n*   **Trigger:** `Ctrl+P` or `:`.\n*   **Function:** Fuzzy search across Files, Container Names, and App Commands (e.g., \"Kill Container\", \"Git Commit\").\n\n---\n\n## 4. 🎨 UX \u0026 Interaction Design\n\n### The Layout System\n*   **Default View:** 3-Pane Split.\n    *   Left (50%): File Explorer.\n    *   Top Right (25%): System Resources.\n    *   Bottom Right (25%): Docker Containers.\n*   **The \"Zoom\" Mechanic:**\n    *   Pressing `Enter` on a focused tile expands it to 100% width/height.\n    *   Pressing `Esc` returns to the split view.\n\n### Keybindings (Vim Standard)\n*   `Tab`: Cycle focus between tiles.\n*   `h/j/k/l`: Navigation within a list.\n*   `?`: Toggle Help Modal.\n*   `Ctrl+c`: Quit.\n\n---\n\n## 5. 💼 Commercial Logic Implementation\n**Strategy:** \"Soft Lock\" / Honor System.\n\n### The License Check (`utils/license.rs`)\n1.  **On Startup:** Check for `~/.config/tiles/license.key`.\n2.  **Verification:**\n    *   If file exists: Verify cryptographic signature (using `ed25519` public key embedded in binary).\n    *   If valid: Set `App.license` to `Commercial(CompanyName)`.\n    *   If missing/invalid: Set `App.license` to `FreeMode`.\n\n### The UI Consequence\n*   **Footer Rendering:**\n    *   If `FreeMode`: Render a text span at the bottom right: `Style::default().fg(DarkGray).content(\"Tiles Free Edition (\u003c5 employees). Support us at dracon.uk\")`.\n    *   If `Commercial`: Render `Style::default().fg(Gold).content(\"Licensed to Acme Corp\")`.\n*   **Features:** All features are accessible in Free Mode (we rely on corporate compliance for revenue, not feature gating).\n\n---\n\n## 6. 🚀 Development Roadmap\n\n### Phase 1: The Skeleton (MVP)\n*   Set up Rust project with `ratatui` + `crossterm`.\n*   Build the `App` struct and the `Layout` logic.\n*   Implement basic keyboard handling (Quit, Switch focus).\n\n### Phase 2: The Data\n*   Implement `System` tile (easiest data source).\n*   Implement `Files` tile (directory walking).\n*   Implement `Docker` tile (connecting to socket).\n\n### Phase 3: The Interactivity\n*   Add the \"Zoom\" function.\n*   Add Docker controls (Start/Stop).\n*   Implement the `license.rs` checker.\n\n### Phase 4: The \"Glue\" (Context)\n*   Make the File selection filter the Docker view.\n*   Add the Command Palette (`Ctrl+P`).\n\n---\n\n## 7. File Structure Proposal\n\n```\nsrc/\n├── main.rs           # Entry point, event loop\n├── app.rs            # State holding\n├── event.rs          # Keyboard/Tick event handling\n├── config.rs         # TOML parsing\n├── license.rs        # Key validation logic\n├── ui/\n│   ├── mod.rs        # Main UI rendering\n│   ├── layout.rs     # Tiling logic\n│   └── theme.rs      # Colors (Dracon branding)\n└── modules/\n    ├── files.rs      # File Manager logic\n    ├── docker.rs     # Bollard integration\n    └── system.rs     # Sysinfo logic\n```\n\n***\n\n### 🤖 Prompt for the AI:\n*\"Take this Master Plan. I want to start with Phase 1. Generate the `cargo.toml` dependencies and the `main.rs` and `app.rs` boilerplate that sets up the Ratatui loop, the 3-pane layout, and the `App` struct with placeholders for the three modules.\"*",
